BRAZIL
METROPOLITAN TRANSPORT DECENTRALIZATION PROJECT
ROLLING STOCK MOTIVE POWER AND WORKSHOPS/DEPOT
1.    This Annex evaluates the Investment Proposal requiremente raised by CBTU
with regard to Rolling Stock and Depot/Workshop maintenance support
facilities. The proposals are designed to improve passenger train set
availability and reliability to meet the planned future increased revenge
service.
2.    Such proposals cover the following &reas: (a) Refurbishment/
modernization of existing passenger train sets (EMU's); (b) replacement/
renovation/refurbilshnent of existing Depot/Workshop equipment; (t) procurement
of additional second hand locomotives; (d) refurbishment of freight cars.
3.    This Annex covers only the needs of CBTU-SP, commenting on its
requirements as listed below. The existing train sets are in average overall
condition but can presently only achieve around 60% service availability.
This substantial shortfall i.s caused by the reasons listed under 5. There io
a shortfall in the number of preventive maintenance Depot facilities to
support train set availability. Proposals to increase such facilities are
covered in this Annex.
4.    The main overhaul Workshops contain a mixture of adequate and run-down
plant, machinery and buildings. As a result of the outdated facilities
productivity is severely affected. The investment sought for the improvement
proposals will raise output significantly.
Rolling Stock Rehabilitation,Proposals and-their O_bectives
5.    Within the Sao Paulo network there are several passenger train sets
presently not ava'.lable for revenue service due to a number of reasons,
mainly: (a) Accident/collision damage; (b) lack of spare parts due to
budgetary restrictions; (c) materiai/components cannibalization, resulting
from (b). These factors significantly reduce the numbers of train sets for
passenger service use (train availability). An ideal service should provide
between 90% - 922 availability. The remaining 8% - 10 is being stopped for
essential maintenance. By investing in the rehabilitation, modernization and
re-equipping proposals studied in this Annex, both networks would raise train
availability figures significantly (see Annex 3 for targets).
6.    Tables 1 and 2 list the train availability statistics for CBTU-SP.
These tables show substantial anticipated increases in train availability
after implementation of the various proposals. The proposals presented to
achieve this, described in this Annex, are straightforward, feasible and
technically sound. CBTU would have to contract out all the work proposed due
to lack of current capacity within their own organization. The work contents
of the proposals are such that a wide range o0 capable Contractors could
submit competitive bids. The Contractors coul.db be Local or International or a
combination involving Joint Ventures or Licenrlng Agreements. The overall
work contents entail mechanical, electrical and civil engineering. The extent
of work, coupled with the quantities involved, would be very attractive to
interested Contractors. Therefore, the bidding should be extremely
competitive.



- 78 _
ANNEX 3D
Page 2 of 8
7.    The issues involving the types of bidding suited to such work have been
discussed in detail. Basically, out of the seven Rolling Stock proposals, six
can be subject to International Competitive Bidding (ICB). This is due to:
(a) Their general scope of work and extent of material/parts supply; (b) the
high quantities involved (13+12+23+14+2+12+5 EMU's).  In this particular case
both the wor', content and component parts supply are specialized. It is
anticipated that the original manufacturer of the train sets could be the only
source able to return those two train sets to their original condition in
order to ensure compatibility with the other sets in the series.
8.    Of the seven rehabilitation/modernization proposals, five involve the
stainless steel carbody shells. Such a factor significantly increases the
justification for renovating instead of replacement by new stock due to their
non-corrosive values and strong construction. This, coupled with the cast
steel bogies, makes the life extension (in the region of 30 years) entirely
feasible.
WorksehonDevot Rehabilitation
9.    The Sao Paulo network is served by strategically sited Workshops and
Depots providing overall train preventive maintenance and heavy overhaul
facilities. However, from site visits to the Depot/Workshops it is readily
seen that extensive re-equipping, renovation and reform work is required to
support the planned passenger train service enhancement program. The sites
visited displayed outdated and run-down machinery, plant, equipment and
working environments in several places.
10.   For example, some of the existing above-floor wheelset lathes are over
30 years old. It was stated that the machine can now only output one wheelset
every two hours. The Mission's cursory examination of the procese would
support this. A modern, equivalent machine should be capable of outputting
wheelsete at the rate of two per hour (4 times output). All the proposals
associated with Depot/Workshop re-equipping and reforming are in the Mission's
opinion entirely justified and overdue. The implementation of the proposals
would create more efficient, effective, safe and attractive work environments.
This would lead to increased train set output required fcr the planned
increased passenger service by significantly reducing the time spent by train
sets under maintenance. Reliability of train sets in revenue service would
also increase. An improved work environment would be an additional benefit.
Table 3 lists the rehabilitation, re-equipping and modernization proposals
identified.
11.   The construction of one new Train Wash Plant is justified.  Presently,
only one mechanized wash plant exists in the system in RJ. To clean the
trains operating on the other corridors, washing by hand at the stabling
sidings is the current practice. This is labor intensive and very
inefficient. The sitings of the proposed Wash Plant has been planned to
handle the e timum numbers of trains with minimum disruption to services.
Acquisition of Second lIand Locomotives
12.   A proposal has been compiled associated with a requirement for eight (8)
second hand 2000 HP locomotives for the SP operations. At present, five
locomotives borrowed from REFSA are used but must be returned.
13.   A need has been identified to increase the existing fleet of five to
eight in order to suipport the planned increased passenger revenue service.
This is for two main reasons: (a) To provide additional support for network
maintenance. This involves Permanent Way and Traction Power Distribution
systems. The additional locomotives are required to ensure adequate



- 79 -
AN^NEX 3D
Page 3 of 8
availability to haul wagons containing materials such as track ballast and
rail for the Civil requirements. For the overhead line power requirements the
locomotives are needed to attend the associated maintenance vehicles; (b) to
provide ready assistance for retrieval of passenger trains stopped in service
thlrough breakdown or s7stem failure. Both these factors have the indirect
effect of: (l) decreasing passenger train headways thus increasing service,
and (ii) providing greater passenger comfort, safety and well-being by better
train ride quality and faster breakdown retrieval.
14.   A study of the numbers of locomotives throughout the CBTU system reveals
that no equivalent specification locomotives are available for transfer to
meet the needs described. The quantities and technical specifications
involved do not lead to foreseen problems/difficulties with regard to
International Competitive Bidding.
Aeuisition Versus Rehabilitation of Equipment
15.   CBTU's proposals are categorized as follows: (a) Passenger Train Set,
(EMUJ)# rehabilitation/refurbishment/modernization; (b) Workshop/Depot,
replacement/reformation/renovation of plant, machinery and equipment;
(c) locomotove, new procurement; (d) freight car refurbishment. Ac'uisition
against rehabilitation can be debated associated with these requirements as
follows:
16.   Passenger Trains - The age of the train set units involved are:
Sao Paulo
Stainless steel   23 EMU Series 101 - 35 years
Stainless steel - 12 EMU Series 160 - 11 years
Stainless steel - 14 EMU Series 400 - 25 years
NOTE: (i) For the 14 Series 400 sets electric traction equipment,
auxiliary energy supply and traction control equipment exist
within CBTU. Such items of equipment would be free-issued to the
successful Contractor; (ii) For the 23 EMU's of Series 101, the
line switches are already available and will be provided by CBTU.
The proposals listed above lend themselves entirely to
rehabilitation work. As mentioned earlier, the stainless steel bodyshells and
the heavy cast steel bogies ensure a prolonged life for the vehicles.
17.   Analysis of each proposal supports the case for refurbishment against
new procurement.  The maitn re-sons being: (a) Faster "delivery" time, thus
providing the proposed increased passenger service earlier; (b) lower
investment cost (around 50%); (c) equivalent car life expectancy.
18.   WORKSHOPS/DEPOTS - From detailed visits to all sites associated with the
proposals, the individual requirements are supported. These are to
replace/reform/renovate/refurbish/renew the run-down, outdated facilities
identified. The implementation of the proposals would contribute to attaining
the designed objective, that is, to increase train set availability for
revenue service.
19.  LOCOMOTIVES - As stated previoualy, it was confirmed that there are no
existing, suitable locomotives anywhere in the system for transfer.
Therefore, the procurement of second-hand locomotives (8 for SP) is juotified.

place.
Workshop/Depot /Re-EauippinelModernization
21.   The 15 individual proposals submitted are divided into the following
categories: (a) New buildings/plant conetruction - 2 proposals; (b) civil

equipment - 8 proposals; (d) refurbishment of plant, machinery and equipment -

Procurement of the Second Hand Diesel-Electric Locomotives
22.   For the procurement of the eight locomotives for SP, CBTU proposes to
use the Technical Specification of the existing five borrowed from RFFSA.
Maintenance Procedes-and Oreanizatioj-
23.   CBTU operates six separate network organizations of which Rio de Janeiro
and Sao Paulo comprise two of these. Each individual network is controlled
separately by similar, independent organizational structures. each



- 81 -
ANNEX 3D
Page 5 of 8
organization is responsible for the day-to-day operations within their own
area. This includes the main operational functions of Traffic, Maintenance,
Finance and Training. From the organizational charts studied along with
detailed discussion with relevant personnel and through site visits, it would
appear that the existing set-ups are adequate for the day-to-day management of
the current operations.
24.   An independent Project Team is located at the Rio de Janeiro Central
Headquarters Offices. This specialist team provides overall support
facilities for all six CBTU network areas. This Project Team were responsible
for the initial identification, investigation, compilation and processing of
the individual proposals covered by this Report.
25.   It is planned that the complete set of proposals, namely: (a) 7 separate
EMU schemes; (b) 15 separate Workshop/Depot schemes; (c) locomotive
procurement; (d) refurbishment of freight cars; when authorized, will be
placed on contract aware more or less simultaneously. Such an overall,
comprehensive plan/program will require extensive, detailed monitor and
control. Such control work will entail the essential project management
aspects of (i) cost, (ii) delivery and (iii) quality. This, coupled with the
extensive day-to-day general communications associated with contract technical
discussion, will require a dedicated, specialist team throughout the entire
project duration (between 2-3 years). Therefore, it is assumed that the CBTU
Central Project Team will be augmented accordingly. This would be by Engineer
grade disciplines specialized in the various proposal disciplines.
Costs and Benefits of the Program
26.   Each  Project Identification form generated covering the Workshop/Depot,
Rolling Stock and Locomotive proposals, contain estimated present day cost
indications.
27.   It can be stated that the eventual overall implementation of the
proposals will improve passenger train availability. This should have the
effect of increasing passenger volumes and the associated revenue earnings
substantially. Service reliability should also improve thus uplifting the
image of the CBTU system. Other benefits include increase passenger safety,
comfort and acceptance.
28.   From a detailed study of the information provided for each proposal
along with discussions held with associated CBTU personnel and site visits, it
would appear that all of the proposals presented for review are reasonable and
justified for the purposes of achieving the proposal performance and
operational targets.
Future Plans/ProRosals
29.   From general observations made during the various Depot/Workshop site
visits, it appears that further similar replacement/refurbishment programs
will need to be generated in the future. It is anticipated that the
implementation of any of the current proposals will not be wasted as a result
of any future similar proposals. Similarly, the majority of the current
proposals are associated with projects within Depots/Workshops sited
strategically throughout the network. Therefore, in the event of any future
rationalization/centralization of activities the current proposals should not
be affected.

BRAZIL
METROPOLITAN TRANSPORT DECENTRALIZATION PROJECT
SIGNALLING, TELECOMMUNICATIONS AND ELECTRIFICATION
SiRna1liuag
1.    Present Situation and Current Programs - The three lines are fitted with
a train interval and operation signalling system allowing for running in both
directions. The equipment is very old and maintenance is difficult. The
network of cables is in very poor condition and suffers from vandalism. At
certain points, the installation of track circuits does not provide for the
required interval.
2.    The SANTOS-JUNDIAI line is equipped with an ATC system using speed steps
(0-20 km/h maximum speed) which does not allow the maximum authorized speed
of the train to be controlled nor to avoid passing through a stop signal. On
the LESTE-TRONCO and LESTE-VARIANTE lines there is no train speed control.
All three lines are fitted .lth a very old centralized control system which is
difficult to maintain.
3.    Recotmmendations - The improvements required to achieve eatisfactory
operation are provided for in the program, for the system capacity required.
In the event of a future increase in capacity, all line equipment would need
to be replaced (track circuits, signals, ATC, etc.).
Proposed Components
4.    (a)   Modification of track circuits arrangement.  The purpose of this
operation is to reinstall track circuits on certain sections of the
network to obtain a minimum interval of 6.5 minutes to achieve the
required system capacity (current interval is 8 minutes). This minimum
interval problem has been noted, but a complete analysis remains to be
carried out. This analysis could be carried out by CBTU-SP staff.
At appraisal, a complete set of specifications was not yet drawn
up. These technical specifications cannot be finalized for the present
60 Hz track circuits, but they should describe the existing ATC system
and provide for proposals for track circuits compatible with this ATC.
This addition on 4 zones leads to 17 track circuits. The list of
equipment point out: (a) use of monorail track circuit which is not
recommendable on main track; (b) similarly, the use of polyethylene
cable is not recommendable because it has no fire protection.
The track circuits removed could be salvaged for maintenance. It
is essential that CBTU-SP draw up these specifications urgently. The
advantage of this operation is to standardize the various possible
minimum intervals in order to achieve maximum equipment efficiency.
(b)   Purchase of point machines.  The purpose of this operation is
two-fold: to increase the number of spare machines in order to improve
preventive maintenance and to replace the crossings controlled by a
single machine, with crossings with one machine per point, by
eliminating the transmission systems and linkages, which are an
important source of faults. This operation will pose one technical
problem. The various types of machines are not directly.



- 86 -
ANNEX 3E
Page 2 of 8
interchangeable. There are differences in machine attachments,
connections to point, locking and control methods.
The problem of crossings can be overcome in two different ways:
either, by converting them into crossings with two machines, as
proposed, or by redesigning a more reliable linkage and transmission
system. It is certain that, with the type of machine used (control and
detection rods) the linkage is complex and that crossings with two
machines would be preferable. This operation will improve availability
by providing for preventive maintenance and by eliminating certain
sensitive installations. Nevertheless, it will not rejuvenate the
remaining stock of point machines which cannot continue to be repaired
for ever. The overall cost seems lightly overestimated. Nevertheless,
as the cost of the modification studies does not appear, we can assume
that this cost will cover the studies and the modification works
realized by the maintenance workshop. Overall, the program provides for
the purchase of 70 point machines. In order to avoid problems of
interchangeability and to facilitate future maintenance, we recommend
that these 70 macliines be allocated to a single line or section and to
use the machines recovered from this section for other areas. On
completion of the program, a survey of the state of installations should
be carried out to determine on which line the new machines should be
installed.
(c)   Replacement of interlocking cables.  The purpose of this operation
is to replace the most severely damaged parts of signalling cable in
order to improve availability and to eliminate risks likely to endanger
safety . Taking into account the installation of cables in ducts and
trenches, it would be preferable to avoid the use of cable with
polyethylene.
(d)   ATS. The purpose of this operation is to require the driver to
perform an action demonstrating his vigilance, at a safe distance from a
stop signal (at maximum speed), to ensure that braking is applied and,
in the event of inadequate braking, to apply the emergency brakes until
the train comes to a halt. The system to be installed is relatively
simple, but it may vary according to the functional specifications to be
drawn up and the required level of safety. Without eliminating driver
responsibility, this system will attract his attention, thus avoiding
several possible accidents.
(e) Signalling for the RFFSA connection at HOOCA. The purpose of this
operation is to ensure the safety of change-overs between RFFSA and
CBTU-SP at MOOCA and to facilitate such change-overs. The improvement
to the signalling system is simple and poses no specific technical
problems. The study remains to be completed. This relatively
inexpensive operation will greatly improve operating conditions and
safety at this connection,
(f)   Signalling for the RPPSA connection at PARATEI.  The purpose of
this operation is to ensure the safety of change-overs between RFFSA and
CBTU-SP at PARATEI and to facilitate such change-overs. The improvement
to the signalling system is simple and poses no specific technical
problems. The text of the joint contract remains to be submitted. This
relatively inexpensive operation will greatly improve operating
conditions and safety at this connection. In addition, it will release
two 24 hour-a day workstations and at least 10 employees. The various
remarks done concerning cables, safety relays and track circuits are
completely applicable. The overall estimate of this item is a 10 X



87 -
ANNEX 3E
Page 3 of 8
lower than our estimate but can be considered as acceptable in this
stage of project.
(g)   Signalling for the MOGI DAS CRUZES to ESTUDANTES stretch.  MOGI
DAS CRUZES is the main terminal station on the LESTE-TRONCO line (only a
few trains continue on to the next station, ESTUDANTES, serving the
University). It, therefore, requires a few parking positions and
operating facilities for arrivals and departures. For the interval of
l8 minutes required at this stage, this terminal station is oversized,
but it is designed for 9 minutes (future stage in increasing system
capacity). The link from this stretch of track to the main track is a
long way from the station and interferes with a level crossing. A
closer connection point would facilitate the management of arrivals and
departures and would simplify signalling for the level crossing.
A comparative study between the proposed system and a simplified
system complying closely with current requirements (interval of 18
minutes), would reveal whether this level of investment is justified,
according to the proposed date for increasing system capacity. As for
the other signalling installations, the program has not been completed.
The program provides for microprocessor interlocking, but the question
has arisen whether convyentional, relay-controlled interlocking would
also be possible. The study proposed above, will show whether it is
possible to reduce the proposed level of investment.
(h)   Centralized Traffic Control.  The three CBTU-SP lines are already
fitted with a centralized control system, the remote control part of
which is very old and subject to many faults. The renewal of the LUZ -
JUNDIAT section is covered by a contract, currently being completed.
The purpose of this operation is to renew the installationo of the rest
of the network. Transmissions will use the main, optical fiber, digital
radio network. Technical analysis has been completed. The technical
sFr'cifications have been drafted and are open for tender. The studies
have been completed. This centralized control is essential to achieve
satisfactory operation. Maintenance of the existing systems is
difficult and is very costly. The cost of maintaining the future system
will be lower.
5,  Comments concerning Proposed Components - These five operations across
the network require the purchase and deployment of equipment such as point
machines, track circuits, signals, etc. In order to retain equipment
standardization provided for interchangeability, CBTU-SP planned to opecify
equipment identical to the present, very old design equipment, which is no
longer in production. Such a decision would lead to a potentially very small
number of suppliers and would ensure that network signalling would remain in
its current archaic state, with high maintenance costs. It is recommended
that the specifications be open to proposals for equipment of modern design
and to install this equipment on one section of the network. The most
appropriate section would be LESTE - TRONCO from ESTUDANTES, MOGI DAS CRUZES.
A survey of existing installations should be carried out to determine the
section of the line to be modernized. This section would be the precursor to
the modernization of the network. The equipment recovered from this section
of the line would be used for operations on the rest of the network and as
spare parts for maintenance. This procedure will result in higher
installation labor costs but should provide for a reduction in equipment
acquisition costs. Above all, it will release CBTU-SP from a technological
constraint and open the way for modernization. A feasibility and
profitability study should be carried out to confirm the viability of this
approach.



- 88 
A&INEX 3E
Page 4 of 8
Telecommunications
6.    Present Situation and Current Programs - The copper cable data
transmission eystems are very old and in such a poor state of repair that
makes them unusable. Six recently installed telephone exchanges are operating
locally# but they are not interconnected becauGe of the poor state of the
transmission network. The other selective and open line telephone systems and
radio networks require modernization and reorganization. The old and poor
quality station loudspeaker equipment from various suppliers does not meet the
requirement of informing passengers. Only 65 of the 180 trains are fitted
with a loudspeaker system which allows the driver to make announcements to the
paosengers. The clock system for stations is installed but is not connected
to the master clock because of the poor condition of the transmission network.
The LUZ and ROOSEVELT control centers are equipped with telephone and radio
communication recorders, but the system is old and does not include time
recording. Only the LUZ station is fitted with a closed-circuit TV system.
7.    Recommendations - A reliable, high capacity transmission network is
essential to enable the other systems to become operational. The various
projects within the program are necessary to achieve satisfactory operation.
Operations provided for withln the Program
8.    (a)   Integrated optical fiber and digital radio telecommunications
system. The purpose of this operation is to equip the entire CBTU-SP
network with a reliable, high capacity transmission system to act as the
backbone for the other operational systems. This system operates with
fixed number of channels using active redundancy techniques. These
channels are used for essential operational linke. It totally overcomes
the problem of electro-magnetic induction which is always very high with
electrical traction systems. It also reduces theft, since optical fiber
cables have little commercial value, unlike copper cables. For the
capacity required, optical fiber links are less expensive than copper
cables .
In terms of capacity, the proposed system complies with CBTU-SP
transmission requirements. The technical specifications have been
drafted and are open for tender. No additional studies are required.
Transmission is clearly an essential part in making the various
operating systems operational. For the optical fiber network the
construction of a multitubular way does not appear to be included in the
rice. For the hertzian network the cost seems lightly over-estimated,
but for such estimate the degree of error is important. It is
recommended that all telecommunication systems (with the exception of
train and station loudspeaker systems) be combined into a single
contract.
(b) Secondary cable network. The purpose of this operation is to
replace the local remote control cables, in poor condition with
underground cables, protected from theft. This operation does not pose
any specific technical difficulties. The technical specifications and
the survey of the cables to be replaced have been completed. The
replacement of cables is essential to achieve a high level of
availability of the various systems. The estimates of the purchasing
costs for cables are acceptable but the costs of the local services seem
high (about twice the price in France for an equivalent service).
(c) Track telephone system. The purpose of this operation is to
create a telephone network (connectors distributed evenly alongside the
tracks) for the use of maintenance teams. The telephone connectors,



- 89 
ANNEX 3E
Page 5 of 8
distributed alongside the tracks, are connected to an existing control
center, via the main remote control system, thus providing links with
the associated CBTU-SP network. The specifications have been completed
and are open for tender. No further stulies are required. This
telephone network will enable maintenance teams to call any part of the
CBTU-SP network for assistance, thus making great savings in travelling
time.
(d)   Track-to-train radio.  The purpose of this operation is to provide
the CBTU-SP network with a radio link between the control center and
train drivers. The present radio network is overloaded and is
unreliable. Nevertheless it is to be retained for maintenance and the
security service (police). The proposed UHF system complies with UIC
and CCIR standards, and will provide the high quality transmission
required for satisfactory operation. The specifications have been
completed and are open for tender. The studies are adequate to issue a
call for tenders.
Ce)   Indication panels.  The purpose of this operation is to equip
large stations with several platforms or junctions, with panels
indicating destinations and departure times. This type of indicator is
very common in public places and poses no technical problems. The
specifications have been completed and are open for tender. No
additional studies are required. This system should improve
company-customer relations, by avoiding the continuous use of the
station loudspeaker system, which passengers find wearing. Technical
data was insufficient to allow an estimate. Nevertheless, the indicated
cost, US$10,000 per panel (without physical and price contingencies), is
acceptable.
(f)   Train loudspeaker equipment.  The purpose of this operation is to
equip all CBTU-SP trains with a loudspeaker system enabling the driver
to make announcements to the passengers and to warn them of the closure
of the doors. The proposed train loudspeaker system presents no
specific technical problemr. Following the TUE series, the work to be
carried out will vary greg ,.y. Certain series are fully equipped,
others already have all t.te train lines required and the internal
wiring. Other series will have to be fitted out in full. The technical
specifications have been completed and are suitable for international
tender. Technical documentation should include the list of components,
with the supplier, together with other possible sources of supply.  The
required documents should enable CBTU-SP to have all, or part of the
system, rebuilt by a third party. The train loudspeaker system is
essential to improve relationships with passengers. However, its use
has not been subject to a great deal of attention. The driver is the
person in contact with the passengers and he should be trained in
communication skills and monitored, since incorrect use of the system
could produce results contrary to those desired. Similarly, the
maintenance of the loudspeaker system should be monitored.   The desired
results are to project a better company image to customers, to make a
significant reduction in vandalism and to improve the regular running of
trains by avoiding delayed departures by ensuring that doors are closed
correctly. The idea of using the system to generate non-operational
income (advertising) should not be adopted, since "audio" advertising is
perceived badly by passengers. The anticipated cost of the
installation, approximately US$4 million, will be recovered with the
first train not destroyed by vandalism. Scheduling should also take
into account the installation of the ATS in some series (LESTE-TRONCO
and LESTE-VARIANTE).



- 90 -
ANNEX 3E
Page 6 of 8
(g)   Station loudspeaker equipment.  The purpose of this operation is
to complete the loudspeaker installation in all stations to enable the
station master to make announcements to passengers and company
personnel. An ins'-allation of this kind presents no specific technical
problems. The technical specifications have been completed and are open
Kor tender. No further studies are required. This operation is
essential to improve CBTU-SP- customer relations, but this will only be
achieved if the equipment is of the highest quality (kept in use) and if
the staff are trained in public address techniques. The idea of using
the system to generate non-operational income (advertising) shLc.d not
be adopted, since "audio" advertising is perceived badly by passengers.
The estimate of costs seems based on a simple installation, non
securised through redundancy.  The relatively low cost of this operation
(US$117,280) and the presence of high quality suppliers in Brazil,
suggests that LCB will be sufficient to promote competitive bidding.
Electrifl4ation
9.   Present Situatiori and Oneoins Programg   -  The general 88kV network power
supply is supplied by two local utilities.  These supplies are in tne process
of being uprated to 138kV. The supply voltage is stepped down to 33 Kv and
distributed, via a dual network, to the transformer and rectifier substations
on the SANTOS - JUNDIAI line. The substations on the LESTE lines are supplied
directly by the utilities. The 4.4 Kv or 6.6 Kv power supply for fixed
installations (mainly signalling,and workshops ) should gradually uprated to
13.2 Kv. Stations are supplied locally from the low voltage network.
10.   Certain sections of lines are supplied at 4.4 Kv from a single network.
This leads to the unavailability of signalling equipment in the event of the
failure of this supply. The switching cubicles are very old and their number
is inadequates particularly on the SANTOS - JUNDIAI line, which results in
long stretches of isolated track in the event of incidents or maintenance
operations. The overhead contact line distribution network is of english
design with rigid mounts. On some sections of the SANTOS - JUNDIAI and LESTE
-VARIANTE lines, the position of the contact wire is obtained by tension rods
common to several adjoining tracks, which results in the paralysis of all
tracks in the event of an incident on one of them or during maintenance
operations, thus preventing temporary single track operation. On certain
sections of the LESTE -TRONCO line, where the track has been replaced, the
overhead contact line is vertically or horizontally out of tolerance,
resulting in incident due to the escape of the pantograph. This type of
installation does not always enable zig-zagging on the overhead contact line,
resulting in rapid wear of the pantographs. Finally, some posts are in very
poor condition, particularly these foundations.
11.   Recommendations -  Of the electrification system as a whole, the network
of overhead contact lines (inclu4ing the switching devices) is most irk need of
overhaul. This is provided for by the program. CBTU-SP should provide for
the possibility of controlling sutation and switching cubicles remotely by
means of the integrated telecommunications system.
Proposed Components
12.   (a)   Physical separation of the overhead network.  The purpose of this
cperation is to make overhead contact lines independent of adjoining
tracks. Technically, this operation consists in installing new overhead
contact line attachments, on posts or gantries, with individual tension
rods for each overhead contact line. The specifications have been
completed and are ready for tender. The studies have been completed.
Down times caused by the collapse of several, adjoining overhead contact



- 91 -
ANNEX 3E
Page 7 of 8
lines should be eliminated. Technically, this operation is identical to
that concerned with the standardization of overhead contact line gauges
(item 3.3) and the two operations should be combined.
(b) ReinstallUtion of the overhead network switching devices. The
-  urpose of this operation is to install switching devices in suitable
locations in order to make best use of the possibility of single track
operation provided by the track and signalling system and not by the
network of overhead contact lines. This consists of installing air gaps
(with disconnecting switches installed on the overhead contact line
supports), close to points and crossings. The specifications have been
completed and are ready for tender.  The studies have been completed.
The reduction in the length of temporary single track will provide much
greater operational flexibility, in the event of overhead contact line
incidents and should also enable maintenance operations to be carried
out on overhead contact lines, without excessively hampering operation.
In order to facilitate the coordination of work, we recommend that this
operation be combined with those described in 3.1 and 3.3, into a single
contract.
(c)   Gauge standardization.  The purpose of this operation is to
replace the present overhead contact line supports with new supports, to
return the overhead contact line to tolerance gauge and to enable
zig-zagging on straight sections of track. Technically, this operation
is similar to that described in (a). The technical specifications have
been completed and are ready for tender. The studies have been
completed.  This operation will lead to a reduction in the number of
pantograph escape incidents and the localized wear of the pantograph.
We recommend that this operatior. be combined with the two previous
operations in a single contract.
flaintenage
13.   Current Overall Structure -  Table D.3 illustrates the current overall
maintenance structure (Signalling, Telecommunications, Electrification)'
14.   Recommendations -  The breakdown according to lines is satisfactory.
The numbder of levels is satisfactory.  The allocation of maintenance teams to
the line is good.  Table D.3 does not take into account workshops and
laboratories which depend on another department. In order to make
responsibilities clear, the relationship between the maintenance department
and workehops and laboratories should be put on a detailed, formal basis. No
maintenance work is sub-contracted owing to the irregularity of resources and
the lack of specialized companies on the market. Most equipment uses old,
electro-magneti technology which, in view of the lack of spare, results in
very rudimentary maintenance. The maintenance and repair workshops are
dispersed and are often in a very poor state of repair. This program include
the grouping of these workshops in a single building which remains to be
built.
15.   Signalling -  Table D.4 illustrates the distribution of maintenance
teams on the line.  This distribution is satisfactory.  The concept of
inspection by a third party does not appear to be applied. However, this is
essential for railway safety equipment.
16.   Telecoiuanications    The advent of electronic equipment fitted with
very large scale integration components will require laboratories to be
equipped with advanced testing equipment (universal automatic test benches).
17.   Electrification - No specific remarks.

METROPOLITA-N TRANSPORT DECENITRALIZATION PROJECT
PROJECT IMPLEMENTATION AND MONITORING
1.    The proposed projeut is scheduled to be implemented over a five year
period and monitored against a targeted time-schedule, starting January 1992
and ending June 30, 1996 (CBTU-SP, Annex 3F - pages 6 to 9 of this Annex), and
against the operational and financial performance targets shown in paragraph
3.22 of the text. With regard to item A Permanent Way, for the rehabilitation
of track infra/superstructure, detailed engineering has been completed and
bids are expected to be called, during April of 1992, and contracts for the
first lots for infrastructure works would be awarded starting in August 1992.
The procurement of materials required for track superstructure works has been
divided into subgroups; the bidding process is scheduled to start in September
of 1992, and the first contracts are to be awarded before July 1992. Works
included in item B, for the rehabilitation and modernization of stations, are
expected to start in September 1992, with completion dates towards mid 1994.
Concerning the Systems component shown as item C (telecommunications,
electrification and signaling), tenders would be called the second quarter of
1992, contracts are expected to be awarded during the latter part of 1992. In
regard to the construction and rehabilitation of workshops and purchase of
equipment included in item D, works would commence in September 1992 and be
completed during the last part of 1993. It is astimated that works for the
modernizationlrehabilitation of rolling stock included as item E, would start
in November of 1992 and be finished by June 1996. The development and
implementation of the various programs, studies and training under item F -
Institutional Development - would start during the second quarter of 1992, and
be completed by end of 1996. Table 1 shows the details of the Procurement
Schedule for major contracts of items to be financed under the loan, and Table
2 the estimated contractual and other payments.
2.    The project would be monitored through quarterly progress reports to be
forwarded to the Bank not later than one month after the end of each quarter,
and through at least two semi-annual meetings between CBTU's management and
the Bank. CBTU would submit quarterly progress reports in format satisfactory
to the Bank, to provide the following information.
A.    Civil and Mechanical Works
(a)   detailed computerized list of the main components, i.e., civil
works, including rehabilitation of permanent way
infra/superstructure, track renewal and construction; stations,
workshops; and installation of electric, signaling and
telecommunication systems; rehabilitation/modernization of EMU's,
wagons and track machinery, indicating contrart' information and
status of implementation in physical and fina. .ial terms;
(b)   summary tables indicating progress versus targets, and expenditure
and loan disbursement status;
(c)   brief description of problems encountered and corrective actions
taken or proposed.



- 94 -
ANNEX 3F
Page 2 of 10
B. Materials and Eguipment
(a)   detailed computerized list of materials and equipment to be
procured, i.e., rails, sleepers, fastenings, ballast, turnouts,
telecommunications, electric and signaling equipment, track and
workshop machinery, indicating the several actions involved in the
procurement process up to contract signature and delivery of goods
and status of implementation in physical and financial terms.
This list would also indicate the projected dates for each action
against actual performance;
(b)   summary tables indicating progress versus targets and expenditure
and loan disbursement status;
(c)   narrative summary highlighting proble4s encountered and actions
taken or proposed.
C. Technical Assistaaie
(a)   assessment of the progress made under each component of the
technical assistance program against agreed schedules and targets;
the identification of the problems encountered and recommendations
for remedial actions; and
(b)   summary of consultants progress reports and contract information
including expenditures and disbursements.
D. Training of Personnel
(a)   a summary of the progress made under each component of the
training program against agreed schedules and targets, the
identification of the problems encountered, and recommendations
for remedial actions;
(b)   updated timetables for training courses, seminars and other
activit.ies with an assessment of progress against set targets; and
(c)   summary of the consultants progress reports, and contract
information including expenditures and disbursements.
E. Traffic and Operational Performance
(a)   an assessment of traffic evolution and a summary of operating
statistics and operational targets agreed
(b)   narrative summary highlighting problems encountered and actions
taken or proposed.
F. Financial Matters
(a) working ratio ;
(b)   salaries and wages as a Z of working costs;
(c)   average train fare;
(d)   paying passengers per day;
3.    In addition, each quarterly report should contain: (a) a summary table
indicating, item by item, the appraisal estimates of costs versus expenditures

and loan disbursements as at the end of the reporting period ia. accordance
with the Project Accounts, and the balance of project loan in accordance with
the respective loan categories; and (b) quarterly movements and the balance
of the Special Accounts; and (c) a summary of loan covenants and their status
of compliance.
4.    In order to monitor the progress of project objectives and provide for
extensive dialogue between representatives of CBTU and the Bank, at least two
semi-annual meetings would be held:
(a)   at the first quarter of each year, the progress made during the
previous year would be reviewed with regard to:
- physical and financial status of CBTU's decentralization project
versus agreed targets, including all components financed under the
project;
- traffic and operations development;
- review of the impact of institutional reforms, and the status of
the action programs;
(b)   during the third quarter of each year, the primary focus would be
upon the next year's program with a review of;
CBTUis budget, and rehabilitation program, considering the level
of overall investments and priorities of the various components;
- evaluation criteria used for investment decisions;
- status of loan covenants.

plans - by November 10 of each year;

budget - by September 30 of each year;
(c)   pluriannual plans for CBTU-SP by December 31 of each project year.
(d)   corporate plan - by June 30, 1992;   and
(e)   revenues, working costs, depreciation and interest for CBTU-SP by
December 31 of each project year.

NETRQ,PL',.q   TRANSPORT DECENTRALIZATION PROJECT
THE IMPACT OF DECENTRALIZATION OF THE CBTU ON STATE
AND MUNICIPAL FINA%NCES
Sumary
1.    The evaluation of the capacity of the state of Sao PQVlo (SP) to assume
the financial burden of the decentralized sub-division has been done
considering the past financial performance in the recent past and the
projected needs of future operating and capital subsidies. In the case of
9BTU-SP, the state's sound financial performance and the comparatively small
magnitude of the subsidy needs indicate that SP may have no problems in
sustaining the sub-division after decentralization.
An Overview of State and Municipal Finances in SP
State of Sao Paulo
2.    In the last 2 years, Sao Paulo State (SP) had net revenues of US$19.3
billion and total expenditures of US$22 billion. The deficit has been financed
by short-run loans, supplier's credits, official credit, and accumulated
arrears. Per capita net revenues show a growing trend (see table 4A.2) over
the last 6 years, although the credit/total revenue ratio has also been
growing, reaching 9% in 1990, compared to 6.2% in 1988.
3.    Total investments financed by SP's treasury (include both inter a.,
intragovernmental capital transfers), that amounted to US$2.9 billion in 1990,
or 12.8% of total expenditures. In per capita terms, they corresponded to
US$88, very close to the average (US$89) for the last 5 years.
4.    The self-financing margin (net revenues less current expenditures),
which is a measure of government current sav^. gsq has declined from US$2.6
billion in 1989 to US$1 billion in 1990, as a result of a US$500 million
reduction in current revenues and a US$1 billion increase in current
expenditures. For this reason, SP could finance 82.4% of its investments with
its current savings in 1989, but only 35.6% in 1990. The wage-bill of the
direct administration corresponded to less than 40% of net revenues in the
last 5 years, although showing a small increase from 1989 to 1990. Altogether,
the hard-to-compress expenditures - salaries, debt service and amortization-
has been below 50% of net revenues, giving flexibility to the state finances.
5.    In 1991, due to the ongoing economic recession, which has resulted from
the macro-adjustment policies introduced by the federal administration, SP's
finance suffered from real reduction of tax revenues, particularly in the last
2 quarters. However, we may expect that, as the national economy recovers, S.
Paulo will resume past growth and so will its fiscal revenues. The impact of
the fiscal changes contained in the new constitution will help S. Paulo's
revenues to regain, in 1992, the 1989 level.



- 104 -
AMNEX 4A
PAGE 2 of 10
Municipality of Sao Paulo
6.    The total revenues of the Municipality of Sao Paulo (MSP), on average,
for the last 2 years, were of US$2.7 billion, against annual average
expenditures of US$3.4 billion. As in the case of other governments, this
deficit is carried over to the following years, compounding the financial
problems. The credit revenue in the last 2 years (Ms Erundina administration)
were, on average, of US$200 million per year, as compared to an average of
US$740 million in the 1987/88 period, the last two years of the former
municipal administration. Nevertheless, the net revenues have increased to an
average of US$2.5 billion in 1989-90, as compared to the US$1.8 billion
average for 1987-88. This is a direct result of the 1988 constitutional tax
reform (whose effects started Jn March 1989) in the municipal finances. The
per capita net revenues have increased from US$158 in 1988 to US$224 in 1990,
and the credit/total revenue ratio has decreased from 31.6% to 7.2% in the
same period. Borrowing as a % of total revenue has remained quite high -
about 50% of the municipality own revenues.
7.    MSP invested US$957 million in 1990 - 60% directly and 40% through its
indirect administration - which corresponded to 27% of total expenditures.
There was a sharp increase if compared to 1989 (only US$391 million). The per
capita investments reached US$85 in 1990, compared to the average of US$77
made by the previous administration during its 1986-88 term. The self-
financing margin that was negative until 1988 became positive from 1989 on,
but the current savings are still too small (an average of US$150 million in
1989-90) to finance a significant share of MSP's investments.
8.    The commitment of net revenues to expenditures on direct administration
salaries and debt service and amortization, has declined from 67% in 1988 to
50% in 1990 - although the direct administration wage-bill increased 56% in
the same period - giving more flexibility to the municipal finance. The intra-
governmental and "other" current transfers amounted to only US$380 million, so
even if most of these expenditures corresponded to indirect labour costs, the
total wage-bill may not exceed 50% of net revenues. The overall financial
situation of MSP should be considered reasonably good, and the country's
present unstable economic situation should not affect its finance with the
same intensity as in the case of large state governments, such as SP and RJ.
MSP, like MRJ, has a much more diversified revenue base - 4 taxes, several
user charges and transfer revenues from both state and federal governments -
than RJ and SP, that basically rely on the state value-added tax (ICMS)
revenue, that is severely affected by both recession and price controls.
Expenditures on Urban Transportation
9.    Considering the annual average governmental expenditures on
transportation as a whole (not only urban) during the past decade, US$1.9
billion were spent by SP (12.7% of its total expenditures).
10.   Although there is no complete information on urban transportation
expenditures by state and municipal governments in Sao Paulo, Tables VI and
VII present a good overall view of what has been spent by the two state
governments in their urban transportation companies.
11.   In SP, the important expenditure costs for the state treasury in urban
transportation correspond to the Metro and to FEPASA. With respect to the rail
company, the figures presented correspond to the overall current transfors
received from SP which are supposed to be subsidising the passenger
transportation operations, since the freight activities are lucrative. Table
VII shows a clear growing trend in urban transportation expenditures made by



- 105 -
ANNEX 4A
PAGE 3 of 10
SP, that have increased from US$335 million in 1987 to US$850 million in 1990.
There are no break-down of information for MSP, that has been spending over
US$500 million per year on transportation, so it is difficult to lcnow exactly
how much CHTC is costing to the municipal treasury. Nevertheless, if a
comparison is made with MRJ, that doesn't carry the burden of operating a
gublic bus system, one can infer that CMTC alone should be responsible for a
high share of NSP's expenditures.
Financial Imnact of Decentralization on State and Municipal Governments
12.   The CBTU-SP rail system to be decentralized required  an operating
subsidy (normalization) of US$70 million in 1990, but as a consequence of the
rehabilitation project, increased traffic and fares, and higher productivity,
these subsidies are forecast to reduce to US$28.2 million by 1993 and to only
US$9.3 million by project completion in 1996. Since SP already runs rail
systems (FEPASA and the Metro), it clearly has the managerial capacity to take
over the new urban rail company, and in terms of costs, the additional US$9.3
million represents a negligible impact. In 1990, SP has spent almost US$200
million on operating subsidies to urban transportation, half of which with the
Metro alone. Furthermore, it should be noted that SP had in 1990 overall
current expenditures of US$16.4 billion, of which US$2.8 billion corresponded
to intra-governmental current transfers, that is, what was passed by the state
treasury as current subsidies to the indirect administration (public companies
and foundations).
13.   Concerning the capital costs of future investments in the new rail
company, it is estimated that, on average, an annual replacement investment of
US$54 million would be needed. Although substantially higher than the
operating subsidies, it is also a small figure if compared to the US$2.8
billion invested by SP in 1990, of which US$650 million corresponded to the
Metro alone. MSP, already overburdened with the costs of CHTC subsidies, will
not have any financial participation in the future metropolitan rail company.

BRAZIL
METROPOLITAN TRANSPORT DECENTRALIZATION PROJECT
URBAN TRANSPORTATION EXPENSES AND HOUSEHOLD INCONE
1.    Although the National Household Survey (PNAD) carried out each year by
IBGE provides more recent data on income and other household features (1989),
compatible data on household income are not available. The last data allowing
a consistent analysis of household income and expenses refer to the period
1987/88 and come from the Family Budget Survey (POF).  The latter was
specifically undertaken by the same IBGE to update the household consumption
baskets on the basis of which Brazilian consumer price indexes are calculated.
2.    Table 1 shows some important variables related to household income and
expenses for S. Paulo metropolitan regions (SPMR).  The regressive features of
the urban transportation costs stand out immediately, as the share of
household income spent in urban transportation decreases as income goes up.
It is interesting to note that in Sao Paulo, where most of the bus system is
publicly run, the degree of regressivity is higher than in Rio, where most of
the bus system is private.
3.    It must be pointed out that in the lower income brackets basic expenses
(excluding urban transportation) exceed average household income by 51% in
SPMR. That is, lower income households spend in food, housing, clothing,
health care and education more than their declared monetary earnings. In the
next bracket, the extent in which household income is committed to those basic
consumption items is also substantially high: 91% in SPMR and 78% in SP. If
urban transportation expenses are added to other "basic" expenses, almost all
household income is used up, even in the 2 to S minimum wage (MW) bracket
case.
4.    For 1991 there is no data available on household expenses, therefore it
was necessary to simulate the share of urban transportation expenses -n the
budget of poor households. Table 2 shows the results of a simple exercise
designed to answer those questions. The month of reference is May 1991, and
the minimum wage, exchange rate, and bus fares are those prevailing at that
time. Households are assumed to have the same size by income bracket as shown
in 1987188 POF. Average household income is assumed to keep the same relation
with the bracket limits as in 1987/88. Household expenses in urban
transportation are estimated assuming that all the household urban
transportation travel are combined bus-rail trips, that 2 rides per day are
made in the 22 working days of the month, and besides that a coefficient equal
to .8 is applied to account for the fact that not all household members make
trips.
5.    Urban transportation expenses as a percentage of household income show
an increase between 1987/88 and 1991.  It is a clear result of the recent
faster increase in bus fares in relation to the minimum wage. The data for
SPMR io particularly representative.of that bus fare growth.
6.    The same exercise can be done to evaluate the impact on low-income
household budgets of the proposed rail rates after CBTU decentralization in
SPMR (US$0.25). An additional assumption has to be made: the minimum wage, by
the time decentralization is completed, will reach the US$100.00 level. This
level for the minimum wage has been repeatedly announced by the government as
one of its major social targets. Actually, if one looks at the recent minimum



- 114 -
ANNEX 4B
Page 2 of 3
wage increase, from US$49.43 in October 1987 to US$84.57 in May 1991, this
assumption seems very plausible.
7.    Table 3 shows that, given the above mentioned assumptions , the proposed
rail fares will take up about 22Z in SP in the lowest income bracket, which
means a substantial increase in relation to the situation portrayed by Table
2. For the households earning between 2 and 5 minimum wages, the increase in
comparison to the current situation is smaller. In the case of combined rides
(rail + bus) the increase is only 4 percentage points for the lowest income
bracket households and less than 2 points for the 2 to 5 MW bracket. If one
is interested in the affordability issue, that is the capability of hougeholds
to pay for their daily urban transportation rides, the fact that the share of
income destined to those rides under the proposed rail fares did not rise very
much if compared to today's situation might be considered quite acceptable.

1BTROOLITAN       PORT DECENTRALIZATION PROJECT
ECONOMIC EVALUATION
1.    The economic evaluation of the project was done for and CBTU-SP as a
whole and by corridor. The evaluation was undertaken for each of the main
CBTU-SP corridors, so as to determ'.ne whether any of the corridors should be
dropped from the project. Some assumptions had to be made in the corridor
analysis insofar as rolling stock is concerned, in order to. artificially
assign it to each corridor, The results are satisfactory and the evaluation
is conservative.
2.    The benefite quantified in the economic evaluotion weres (a) direct
benefits ouch as the reduction of trip cost and the value of time savings
reduction of the road maintenance cost due to lesser buses, reduction of the
operating costs associated with the traffic control of buses; (b) indirect
benefits such as the reduction of congestion due to lesser buses, reduction of
road accidents and the reduct4.on of environmental pollution. The indirect
benefits were not included in the base cases evaluated. They were only used
for sensitivity analysis purposes. The costs quantified in the economic
analysis weres (a) the long-run marginal costs of the CBTU operation which
were estimated using standard costs to reflect less erratic maintenance
policies; and (b) the economic investment costs of the program.
3.    The sensitivity analysis on traffic forecasts, increased investment
costs, deferral of benefits to the fourth year, etc., produced acceptable
results which ranged from 22.2 to 58.2% for CBTU-SP. Next, let us examine in
detail the economic evaluation for each of the systems.
4.    The basic inputs used for this economic evaluation are summarized in
Table 3. The analysis was undertaken by corridor and for the overall network
comparing the situation with and without project. The ERRs for each corridor
and for the overall network are given in Table 1. The sensitivity analysis is
summarized in Table 2. Overall, the S&o Paulo component has an ERR of 46.7%
for the base case. Table 2 shows the results of the sensitivity analysis by
corridor. Cash flows are given in Tables 7 and 7.A,
Global
5.    The ERR for CBTU-SP was estimated at 46.7%.  Cash flows with and without
externalities are given in the following pages. Details of the analysis, such
as the computation of each of the benefits and costs, are described in Report
No.20, which exists in the Project File.

ANNEX 5B

BRAZIL
METROPOLITAN TRANSPORT DECENTRALIZATION PROJECT
FINANCIAL EVALUATION
Summary of Conclusions Drawn From Proiections
General
1.    The proposed project finances the investment required by CBTU-SP to meet
the operational and financial targets set in Annex 2.
Sao Paulo (CBTU-SP)
2.    The combination of tariff increases, increased passengers and cost
reductions are projected to decrease the operating subsidies from US$ 70.3
million in 1990 (US$ .27 per paying passenger) to US$ 9 million in 1996
(US$.03 per paying passenger). The working costs are forecasted to decrease
from 4.3 times revenues to 1.1 times revenues. Additional ridership and
increased fares after 1996 could continue the performance improvement.
._of-Proiect A sumDtio
3.    The accompanying financial projections of CBTU-SP are based on the
following assumptions:
Decentralization Assumptions
4.    The urban rail transport system of Sao Paulo (CBTU-SP) will be
transferred to the state government free of debt and prior liabilities. All
subsidies received for operating costs and capital additions (including the
World Bank project) will be the responsibility of the federal government until
the decentralization is completed. The division of these subsidies subsequent
to decentralization among government levels will be negotiated at a future
date, except for future debt service requirements existing at the time of
decentralization which will remain a federal obligation until this debt is
cancelled.
5.    The assets transferred constitute the rail systems of the two cities
operated by CBTU.
Financial Assumptions-Income Statements
6.    The projections are based on the 1990 actual results projected to the
year 2001 in accordance with the assumptions listed below. Results for 1990
for both systems were converted into dollars at the average exchange rate for
1990 of CR$ 68.55 per US$ 1.00. The Project is assumed to begin during 1992
and continue until 1996.
Farebox Revenues and Other Revenues
7.     The passenger generated revenues were projected by assuming increases
on transported passengers, reduction of fare evasion and tariff increases,
that by the time the project is completed in 1996, will have reached 90% of
the modal (most common) bus fares in both cities. These projections (Table 6)
conservatively assume that the number of paying passengers and tariffs will
not increase after 1996. Other revenues for rents and other services are



- 123 -
ANNEX 5B
Page 2 of 12
projected from historical amounts, and because they are not material to
results, are subtracted from other expenses in the income statement
projections.
Operating Subsidy
8.     The operating subsidy is the difference between farebox revenues and
working costs and consequently, does not provide for capital additions or debt
service.
Salaries and Wages
9.     Salaries and wages were projected based on the 1990 wage-bill and
adjusted for personnel reductions that began in May 1990, continues in 1991 as
this report issues (July 1991) and is expected to continue though 1995, when
CBTU forecasts an increase in maintenance personnel needed as ridership
increases. Details of forecasted salaries and wages are attached in Table
6.A.
Electricity
10.   Electricity costs were projected according to the consumption of car x
Km/month observed in 1989, the projected increases of the car x Km/month and
electricity rates of March 1991. These projections are presented in Table
5.A.
Spares and Materials for Maintenance
11.   Spares and materials expenses for maintenance were projected based on
89/90 values, increased by 10% for CBTU-SP, management's estimates of the
1989/90 under maintenance. Projections beyond 1991 were based on the
forecasted increases of car x Km/month and are presented in Table 6.B
Other Working Costs
12.    The other working costs were projected as percentages of the total
working expenses based on 89/90 values. For Rio it was assumed that they will
decrease slightly, but in Sao Paulo a small growth is expected, since many of
the services there are contracted with outside firms. These projections are
presented in Tables 5.
Depreciation
13.   The depreciation not based on undervalued CBTU carrying costs for its
substantially depreciated fixed assets, but is an estimate of depreciation
based on current replacement values as shown in this Annex 8-15 and 16.
Interest
14. Since the federal government assumes all existing debt burden before and
after decentralization, the projections do not include any provision for
interest. For comparison purposes, the 1990 income statements exclude inter-
est with a corresponding reduction in the operating subsidy.
Other Costs. Net
15. Other costs include provisions for accident or labor claims incurred
after decentralization and other various minor costs, net of miscellaneous
revenues.



- 124 -
ANNEX 5B
Page 3 of 12
Financial Assumptions-Statements of Sources and Application of Futnds
16.   The source and application of funds consolidates the funds produced by
the independent systems with additional funds required to maintain the
transport system.
Other Sources
17.   The other sources consist of the proceeds from the World Bank project
loan and capital subsidies for:
a.    Federal government counterpart funds for the project.
b.    Capital addition requirements not financed by the World Bank
c.    Debt service for existing loans (interest and capital)
d.    Debt service for the World Bank loan (interest and capital)
Investments
18.   The investments for 1992-1996 are the estimate of the capital addition
requirements not financed by the project of the two systems during the project
implementation period. For the years 1997-2001 these amounts decrease to an
estimate of capital additions required to maintain the renovated systems.
Interest and Amortization
19.   These amounts are based on management supplied information of debt
service to maturity of existing loans and the proposed World Bank loan.

ANNEX 5C
Page 1 of 2
BRAZIL
METROPOLITAN TRANSPORT DECENTRALIZATION PROJECT
ENVIRONMENTAL IMPACT OF THE PROJECT
1.    Since the main objective of the proposed project is to increase the
capacity offered by the rail suburban system, it is expected that a
substantial percentage of the passengers now carried by bus will return to
their original mode of transportation, that is, rail. This is especially true
for passengers who live within walking distance from the stations, who
switched to bus because, in the last five years, the capacity offered by the
trains decreased considerably. However, it is not so obvious for those
passengers who are not within walking distance. Nevertheless, it is estimated
that in the Sao Paulo metropolitan area there will be 1006 less bus tripsiday,
because 320,000 pass/day will switch back to rail. The main positive
environmental impacts expected stem from this reduction in bus services, given
their present negative impact on the air quality, noise levels, traffic
congestion, road accidents. Other positive impacts are the effect of the
rehabilitation of the rail system on passenger safety at the stations, on the
land use around the right of way and the decrease of fatal accidents resulting
from lack of fencing of the right-of-way. We will discuss these impacts in
the next sections.
2.    The impact on air quality is due to lesser fumes produced by the buses
which will be removed from circulation, or which will have their route-km.
shortened because they will be feeding the trains rather than running parallel
to them. The impact on air quality was estimated at 6.3 million US$/year in
Sao Paulo. The impact on noise levels is also due to the removal of buses,
where the vehicles are noisy and when bunched together, cause very high db
levels, which hardly allow people to chat at normal voice levels on the
street. This impact was quantified at 1.3 million US$/year in S. Paulo. The
impact on traffic congestion was also estimated at 8.4 million US$/year in S.
Paulo and is mainly due to the lower waiting time for commuters using their
automobiles and buses and also due to the savings in fuel consumption since
the vehicles consume more when they are idle. The effect on road accidents is
based on statistics which suggest that in these metropolitan regions the
number of bus accidents is estimated at a certain level. It is estimated that
the savings due to lesser accidents are 1.7 million US$/year in S. Paulo. In
addition, the fencing of the right-of-way is expected to decrease the number
of fatal accidents due to people who are constantly trying to cross the right
of way. References CB18-19-20 of the Project File (Annex 6) describe the unit
values used to quantify the benefits and costs.
3.    Benefits which were not quantified are those related to the improved
living environment which will result from safer and cleaner stations in Rio,
crossovers from the sidewalks to the stations, space for queuing up at the
wickets, ramps for the handicapped and, in some cases, modal integration with
taxis, buses and private automobiles. Other non-quantified benefits are those
related to the structuring effect of a revamped rail system which will attract
housing in the surrounding areas. Furthermore, real estate development on the
air space above the stations and in land owned by CBTUJ is also expected.
Otlher non-quantified benefits relate to the lesser stress which the road
system and congestion will impart on the road users and the better ambience
expected in trains where, at present, people are carried as cattle. Lower
trip times and faster home-to-work trips may also have a more negligible
effect on the rail users' welfare.



- 135 -
ANNEX 5C
Page 2 of 2
4.     The proposed physical rehabilitation of the system is not expected to
have negative impacts on the environment. Most materials used will not affect
nature, the contractors will be responsible for proper disposal of old
materials, the earthworks are mainly in CBTU's existing right-of-way and there
is no expropriation. Wooden ties will only be procured from contractors who
are allowed by X-heir national agencies to sell them and wherever feasible
concrete ties will be used. The visual impact of the stations will be
minimized with proper architectural designs which will blend with the
environment and the same will be done with the overhead catenary, wherever
possible.
5.     In short,  the environmental impact of the project is expected to be
highly positive and even in the worst scenario, if passenger projections do
not materialize, it will still be positive for the metropolitan regions
involved.

CBTU FAST DISBURSEMENT ALTERNATIVE
1.  CBTU believes that it can disburse faster than proposed and agreed with
the Bank. The Bank has no objection in anticipating disbursements if CBTU
complies with all Bank guidelines for procurement of works, goods and
consultants.
2.  Accordingly, the Bank has agreed to include in this appraisal the
Disbursement Schedule proposed by CBTU.
